Facebook Display Ads


More stats have been released saying Facebook is the display impression king. comScore says Facebook had 27.9% of all the world's display ad placements by the end of 2011 - up 6% in a year. Yahoo! (11%) and Google (5%) and Microsoft (5%) finished second and tied for third, respectively, says comScore. Read more in the WSJ (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmkJo4b8mqH_Jin4o_mbeoITzd7DPXN7FJZBB7JU7WuHnb1AYJTiN3U76CK2nWMJB9yooW5QayPjvHnO2VrxDsS5kaeE43Dc2-WisainkT6mxuDBT11dSw2Qhw6FVRBJIPTitoqIE1g62E35IYuCxqtlrXIWJozvrBm4glYrJtW7NYdWHSS64Y8hXH5VvD9TSd8UwCY47CCbePq6tvrhFkxrA0z9JLSLs5wENfooKqnP8yUuQRzM1ecbsEzxo5FrU-CwAVlISMHJ6E_cXiroTv5pY5nbvsObAkuVeInNptpPJIcj7G8ZgsNJuGE3AYhNwIynm2SVFFMRDw==> . Looking at the display dollars, eMarketer has estimated Facebook cranked out $3.8 billion in ad revenue last year. On its last earnings call, Google said it made $5 billion <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmm3znigtMWytpHQPkm4hv_awPxKn7EG-w577fA9_14G5gRrYkbWqmWmdXIl1DIXQccVUO_dyqq_GN14hdcBZOTZm-KJ60jgeDhA3-R4Cty1iA-9NmjQTbrtRLakEn2RbGVbCLH_8O2Wp0pLsUrY86ar7VjMc2ykW1u72DU_1xYk7rhhslSXmsb0mdN_Vhy7OpBCgRa_PLTCATmSG5W1QrqlZkfFYewzsY9dsx5KzrxKb_GrEJo3fAAWPiGaODQPKUgUW8hJbfounw==>  in display revenue last year. Who's really in the lead? Depends. 


Brand Safety Dance


Everyone's doing the brand safety dance <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmlMuwWiJwGZNo4cL5SlRXTFUfaDodyz-PrxtEMnW4CW02ZOuSn_W9y7be-nsU_4nbWatXh3KELTv89k_vAA9lugf9OSimQhvMQFvdLzPXFW1g83CdgLECEytiBQwuWkCXoHduJ9FoWUyQ==>  as TubeMogul announced that it will be scanning web pages for inappropriate content before placing ads. According to the release, its new BrandSafe technology "will be built into every buy on its real-time media buying platform," and assist in reducing the problem of badly placed online video ads." Proximic will provide the contextual page scan for TubeMogul as semantic tech continues to be a component of the ad verification world. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmlHe-PtMjSRSSa2uG8xv5YEjv4ecyCL-ULPMRpa3zWlGK_Xzp173QToohm-Vcd_pys-8AiJK81yKnPPctPbN5elAP7e9HSeOt9lWfImbmaG_WtzNMV1PN7pckZHprVPlAmUVp-9ZGXMyVLPwPG-m2mHVPruMcxvP5xDm45bZ5KUJflHiwz6jcxff0kxYgoXnm5gWSf925e8e0QJ0fq7qszlYWDQMluGlGOYt3q5EabLmFxY3wkNPJIX6GDktc-7kmz6oiB8Nhfw0gVwabKqVzEM2fuPjQWBT__b6OSYhQat-ywNb0Q4HAM4lhOgcOOcRR__1a3fQnd0u6Zh5-1ugbgACEu5N9ldQnLQBO6aZEZfERGO-ZWNZK08>  Another interesting data point from the company regarding its pre-roll "sniffing" technology - it says it has blocked over 653 million fake pre-roll impressions. Meaning auto-play stuff. 


Monetating


It's earnings season and landing page optimizer Monetate has decided to offer a bit of insight on how it's faring even though it's a private company. The company claims a 278% increase in annual revenue growth. In addition, the company says in a press release that it "is in the midst of an aggressive hiring campaign that will double its service and support staff in 2012." There's more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmniRf-__Sfni_mkPRYrCcJNWcOX-S9XcA8JWfpobG2ZSPKVfrJcD064PYG26Gi3vITaUFV2T_jHi0FsGs1xcgc30X9Rwf2oiOxDTPTHcrCzbvOKZFod1Dj9ZRGazfHE63k7Pwjv3B9mFjmWWQYLLK5ld9HkhVWj9jTaeCEIuQnKGjyXyJJTFOauffiPReH2ROIE-B-C4A0kNs9nzyieOnXKSB6TtPPz07sLutMkvHm5W6YWop6117iILgUr6rzT9hh1qXEBKOZMxg==>  The company had received $15 million <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmlxbnBTtmmVl0xDeg-XRBgTGwwv7NWGQAukflKm2uXCEskRF4wQlfKcovOOscmT1CyTYjPrfjWFa5aKPz2jkachIvu1PDFHyHqT9ifjdWpuKxfpul-4qcNJgKn7t2hPPi5Pn-xz4dOu7iAghgboHKistD-QPsac-wwLGxIN3pyxy_o2vhX-Cqmbm1IsWtrwpAB7AqRXMaJ2F5-6LKrF2axtBmwvYwpa0yRc4tzurdHCV4ox0p7NxeXX7d6WfQeFCjxlcjAx7t37nQ==>  in August to grow the company - including its staff. 


Caller, Are You There?


Pew Research says, "More than half of adult cell phone owners used their cell phones while they were in a store during the 2011 holiday season to seek help with purchasing decisions." Read more mobile data <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmmwbdEc95xMz8oC9hDD14M8VKQWuAMr0VGql8nv7Aqfcfyzwui0ZGc0sr2T61U1vNwJDr58p2pokrB-W6VdlrfptXApIIJdltZOX5a-JS93BnMNuYRf3AaoLrkLgSivSkZJahsRO7IosxOJCww-dOiqBJOrgPvgzd6ZmOkZWjGl2VWnLLjS1nZp81x65u8xy0c6rRKE4vfxGg-4AVB0eBM7I8_0LYHXe9fF99w9dgvkRxgFoeCR1LXNqDbBSQrsTg0kHFFHOODmZrkLkDkIOzhvI2CAgtg11co=> . Pew says a third of those calls were part of a growing and powerful trend that retailers such as Target have called "showrooming" (WSJ <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmmz3CjFwDKs9P-CxwD8e2hL-sfTwyp_d2SYHgFq7sWqUjRigQv0OPX95Mb9En763EuFSPhCUPpS7MGvkkq3GJTIp7Lg21AFbwQ0xgDz8cvMMVZplfdQdP1KSUWnBKbEU2TjE8c_qpHx58ZHqh3Yv0qdJayAhVMwmc0jI-GaMM8iUsG-UP0-kTh7scLzb_EFecSOyXHgrfFf-UD_OfYS1hFIToh9thiGPsQclrKQqltGJagVjw7SjnV6fyjtlzLsBDzcL4Prq0NE6xZVWpdyeZD2Xd_A7HbS4F0=> ) where users comparison shop online - while in the store. 


Cookies And The Law


Adweek's Katy Bachman reports that U.S. Congressman Ed Markey is creating new legislation specifically for mobile after news of GPS tracking in some mobile devices. Bachman writes, "The Mobile Device Privacy Act would require companies to let consumers know what types of information are being collected, which companies get the information and how the data are being used. It would also require companies to get consent from consumers before information is collected, shared or transmitted." Read about it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmmwos_8aHsdNuim4xwYMTQac4EF3YM96g5k_OB76Gsq0gF7cX9fgd8BmEfIlIBPQeW-q70ew4FR7bIdZ27iy4mRoPSZYj45S_B5ceZXd2E2-LzLcXJLXJMNUiDUcta37f4tUSnNkwa5gE8QQEeIL7bjmEf2cAcFBeOCGg4F2_ZZBbuvTBuX1yrX7EsyyP7ZqakBMU6eyvsF4VMwrQHnPtwaiKmlJQ85ZI7-uxtjUN0T83ax8E-eTUdoh9bSV1HZIbZjZxX0-JTcGMQKQZXLNkphjV7fPF9SiB8=>  Meanwhile, BlueCava announced its bringing its cookie-less, device ID technology to the European Union as regulation swirls. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmkshC6_HrrGW2OZ-GbSfCrp9L4p1ME71_cJiT631tiWIYzPYJ1s4F0ziL20V35vLNXp8w0rqIpBaG1dewE9K4AobruEDAaABd0WF37wY18j46aofZ26S3sJSrOK8K5GvAQj9upcdqzkz9aGBsEEGUTDCYE7iBFbcbnWyWA3khQkAYMvNDrV2HTwjDXbAm8dtmhpy6_mNsKupG8qXWfQ3tKFNXa6HyqRewjBynu6uqLJyrOtXfWChN_ZZ-mdaonsHDwfl-OH3S8fFQ==> .

Upward And Onward


Down under, Australian display advertising leader ninemsn (a venture of Microsoft and Nine Entertainment in Australia) said that it saw a small increase profit for its news portal while revenues grew nearly 30% last year. ninemsn CEO Mark Britt said, "In 2012, we are watching the economy and market with interest, but expect ninemsn's results to continue to be strong, as online advertising continues to take revenue share from other media as it catches up to the Internet's share of the time people spending using media." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109178600177&s=8442&e=001QSHV2xRcJmkS_N54v3JssnsPlbd-eYz2vmsMguTrhTWJeSZpLSJ_zF8BV8PhgF4fLxboux6FwcuzbzxkDwOPJx8Gn4zr_cOCtMF-bCntfq7LVc9hOAX6JUr8KGswyKQYmwcvzcEtAcj_JY24aaFXlrj7h8PuK7miq09sNdVpMK7ROlttmfJScytdDpJiTlMyz2d33485DoKd5bnBPwzTPO34FcAZwKSzHBZYbJYZcrVkwGUoMNG-lW8RO9jwpKCT7VD9KdOCJXui6es7FkoloO_ixLGBBJ5aDGecaqujgUtHVMMm7lEqxete0hP3o6rM-QIZ00hmo3LamPSHHXuGHKNbkpKojZ-w> . 


No Longer Demanding


paidContent's Ingrid Lunden reports that Demand Media has seen steady exit of senior level executives. Founders and EVPs Larry Fitzgibbon, Joe Perez, and Steven Kydd will leave the company says Lunden. Is this anything more than entrepreneurs vesting, or meeting earn out requirements, and then leaving after their company has been acquired? *	Data-Driven Thinking: Taking Issue With Viewable Impressions by Mark Hughes, CEO, C3 Metrics <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109160057406&s=8442&e=001LWh26IE3E_Iobc75946MsfFJqjg5ZnsVAc4iRRC2JXbqeBBInKhp5a4xMLLBm11JACErR3u67DsjGYMCXfj1UFAoc9MgzC1qnViCspA7MwR3fRBqlmuyw57LT3aVFAAUaHlAqPg93UMcQKXSuUw64jr5egCW7qfLgGk9UVPwMH4a3AWYW8BpyEmmnk4bkNCyB2r7JlFSFrXUUgcOYlITynm8YGn8H1UbzeS5_1g9rraprX4nDZ1dfwh7_8vYee2iWZqlYEE2REXQIOyXk6AnNg==>  "I would like to see two actions result from this divergent discrepancy. First, click-through rates must be calculated on impressions viewed, not server requests. Second, attribution modeling, which is critical to display success, must also incorporate the viewable impression standard, because view-through credit is entirely based on an actual view. As a result, CPMs for viewable impressions will justifiably rise, and unviewed impressions will no longer count in display ad performance reporting..." (visit AdExchanger.com)

Like IPOs?


The monster initial public offering from Facebook is almost here. The Wall Street Journal says the company is expected to file the necessary papers this week which is expected to put a $100 billion, public market valuation on the company in the not-too-distant future. Think of the millionaires floating around Facebook offices! - you know who you are. The WSJ says, "A $10 billion Facebook offering would rank fourth among IPOs for U.S. companies, behind Visa Inc., General Motors Co. and AT&T Wireless." What are they going to do with all that company cash? Read it (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109160057406&s=8442&e=001LWh26IE3E_LmvxRmfsfTeCstPHokL8NROaIrjVIy_JSx9d-rMi9r9MHDlJeLSDrPsLzFqLQaWyUCkcVEE3Mn38Rr2EWl0Bl0uBE_-1EgI440AYLZY92o6Vyf0ULhADOs1M0K8sBRFw0AdrsT3GpOe2i_SrHgURtw2BIJijdMfR4MGS9ihxDmZ-lpvOJUeI-lfSTniOfTRaJo5BxmZRgRi-rV85JCWkoTULzAahe_rVGVDtXIwJspzETVAQD5lYG5z8-Hi58PvE3yRTKdA9kUT6wDz5c3LvQ8UYK36xP9BybjYWQSy2uxFQCZgiJ7P_AUkhYZ5if9NCkT10XTLpWCpg==> . Could Facebook some ad tech?  Seems FB often buys companies for the people, not the tech. 
 
P&G Banking On Digital


Another seminal moment in marketing? Consumer-package goods company Procter & Gamble will throw caution to the digital wind. Last Friday, Ad Age's Jack Neff reports on P&G's earnings conference call and says that flat results have led to plans for the elimination of 1,600 non-manufacturing jobs as it steers toward a digital marketing future. Chairman CEO Bob McDonald says, "In the digital space, with things like Facebook and Google and others, we find that return on investment of the advertising when properly designed, when the big idea is there, can be much more efficient." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109160057406&s=8442&e=001LWh26IE3E_IyfK_V3UI8P-mpX9cqJlWAJLZZsB48qVkx65VfQyYzyKWzGFd4n95u_z41Fw5E7wrb2VI_3VLDpQluE_bExLoIjXbH_i4_GYjKBupvAeKD7nFRixdpV0D_uBz2Ik7zS6Ve78Ih4Mx0UOk4IUycwhE4AA4tiu3tUdmeGP3TBU-FYeqAiEZzHMejbvpwg_7ESiuryMM-6I3l4xJAw7ziTWR1CctnNoPYz2kslxwsXRxLPNm-Kw-Z2ywL7GtZ2NG8dgkNoxbVkx83I4nf5e-eOJQZ3E4sNuuh586gLgZiemBcpf8zwTmh1y6X> . 


Retargeting Mobile Engagement


As mobile ad network Millennial Media edges toward its IPO, it continues to roll-out new products as mobile engagement appears to be a problem it's looking to solve. According to a press release, the company's new "App Engagement Program" gives marketers an ability to "anonymously identify consumers who have already downloaded their app, and use mobile display creative to deep-link these users back into the app." It's unclear from the release exactly how Millennial is retargeting users, but with privacy concerns circling the mobile cookie, Millennial's solution could be attractive to marketers. Read more.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109160057406&s=8442&e=001LWh26IE3E_KxRBaqe3Jv427p9GiAFie3MD5jpuwcwbJsllDAbWdOMpNMF1J8Y_ViCOeTBAW74YC4zTH6mjT3J_AOYN61Ya6yROBd4vA67H4O6mWhddT3PzsOWU6d6jbSjvEP5PDd7PKNbyIrBCYbzGLx8WN9kxqOhiQuWVuSs9Zo-jYjfJvhPxzslxtGPsH1UfENKeC_oyXkt4vSa-7EEFDR1mzSGWvfxjwCZ4fuCSo8C1OFtetg_C_1ceE_IWDV3k0X-DyTcjXHoJPfaO0Ur48r1JfwnDJhtJDk-SO20570iYGEKA8ki80W_4teCjbPK2CDhy0Rsb-OIU_htlArS96uv-tSDkFG> 


Media Flow


iCrossing SVP of strategy and planning Gary Stein takes note of the latest eMarketer stats <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109160057406&s=8442&e=001LWh26IE3E_I-BS1h6CDQmWxjKKrmHt2CTNyUwl0Fufh9WM4YjOOMSH0bbRuj63GBJK60FTbqWQ9dwVjWvVVKWsu0OKrdzFmmpzEKG7fbzGjNVG5owxxyaNmcQZ-Daon8UNwki-ZQEV4kp4g1f0vnLPz653wIfNvHEpszjwNfJlfHP1BaHQiGWDxvq7Uw5tZ1Aa0URqribpv7Z5HErrUekhpS_RZTE5fqd8Sh27oSYx6Jg1d3c_KiKohFbiGq4C27AtZuPDsZIjaSJfmvSRhqOvQMTvNr5mlSN_i1zLqtJEc=>  as online overtakes print spend. He says that media companies can't position around one channel any longer: "ESPN used to be in the business of running a cable channel. Today it's in the business of keeping you deep inside sports. The New York Times used to be the newspaper of record. Now it's the deepest and most trusted source of news and information." Channels are "overflowing" into each other says Stein. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109160057406&s=8442&e=001LWh26IE3E_KLDCpq7eNQSV4pXvIkzW1iSDZZ7-NLBYZMnXrw08603rkxCqNg3mGQZbHOQGSw_JwPA-CH75Le_PeOIpwAo7V8b4rhQjRE2UVxvmy5wOGUKCRKV2gvHjQkqr1zF0jS4KhOBMZggPNntpA246jXgULQJRPynK0N1iKk5Uz7gsadwDttbi8pmtjT-IJ4Ux6PV4TO_3by2FNjhIatHM_nKR4jDySmmJhd5AkoUGwcckx5azvcPGuBVS_b3Pe0td75_fwiiQIlCNVThzO-isguoxjAcMHkhLplxlCh31dYluKl5g==>  


Targeting Scanability


GRP Partners' and VC Mark Suster outlines many of mobile's attractive attributes, but reminds entrepreneurs - and buyers and sellers of mobile and Web-based online media - not to get drunk on it. On the positive side for mobile, he says users are "more likely to be the 'bottom end of the sales funnel' or in other words close to 'point of purchase.'" On other hand, you can't scan long reviews of restaurants, for example, on mobile like you can on the PC. The Web has its place - read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109160057406&s=8442&e=001LWh26IE3E_L0reeA2IUyFbzt5b2eSifv64RvNWbzA1QGd3fyXHLLcuwFOc1Dc0tJ5pz15RRnKZZd6F5eY9oyA7j7pdZOCz8dRHNAAG-Y9PRWvObmlf8NPeNY7JdTmKJneXdSvyqNDUT60lvAPM7pwW_EgOqkAvowzJHpEkbrGRlQW1bWMMCZW01vRW022MC2zxZ7IwmnizEyt-DWbJG8EVUoe03fk5batSRxuI0oX2R4rdMHh_Y-xY8cKZf5OJJQg4ORDYQ0JhMfRZnOx8nLVB_cNF74u6gXnesU_XxWMX8=> . This sounds like a similar argument between scanning the content of the newspaper and a web page. Lean back and think about it. Now, lean forward. The more scannable, the higher in the funnel you can target?

Culture And The Company


What's your company culture like? Do you even care? You should says an article by Shawn Parr in Fast Company. The benefits of an "alive" culture to a company and its people are vast including better focus, more motivation, cohesion within the team and something Parr identifies as "Spirit" which he says "Shapes employee behavior at work, enabling the organization to be more efficient and alive." Read more about culture. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109160057406&s=8442&e=001LWh26IE3E_Jyera--jRECPVf20mJAFTLVnhmah-4dAKOV7QzBeTJWmf6o8-aTRTViX2yqBPt2enwRljt3ctpdNq028Ux1cXJEcblpzKYkYAEa8ecM1banWCrNLi0sXSOsfUR9wNiiOXjeXSdxrSOLsltOlK2-afDMJu9fK1DRVLuQWYBS0_DD8eRNYSYAMSGLfd7suejFSLrGUcIP_J_NR0J-19CAqBzaf0QBc59qQ8uvktg5LQjSOL30GPUddj5Bj_v1N-QFulafJatOMG-_A==>  


Google+ Wins


Signal is pouring off of websites which embed various social share buttons like badges of Web honor. On TechCrunch, Binnu Reddy takes the weekend microphone and says that Google and its Google+ button can still win the social sharing game if it can get us all to share publicly - so not just sharing to our media buddies, but everyone! Reddy writes, "In order to make public sharing universal, user behaviour needs to change dramatically. The good news is that Google touches pretty much every Internet user and is in a great position to make this happen. Here are some ideas on how they can do this: 1. Help people build a meaningful audience..." Predicting Content Gets Funds


Dennis Mortensen's Visual Revenue has received $1.7 million in new funding to continue to grow the business and work on the tech which optimizes the publisher's front page. Managing yield starts with the content from Visual Revenue's perspective. According to the release, "[Visual Revenue's] solution can predict the performance of a piece of content about 15 minutes into the future and provides editors with real-time recommendations on what content to place in which position on a Front Page and for how long." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV04hrI8VNU9M7L2WLoWDcnPkiWgTEbesrcqd1ZF0aQn5iLxdXRoGl-XYIepNqM1g305mifCWlBRX8OMil3eGTvjJJAkXyLSnScueGLNdl5Tx9WjeQlYd8rqQD-Ru-PQRPD7aLTT9Chjz6xpb-oZ4ipWs>  $1.7 million feels like a bridge loan - not a whole heckuva lot. Could there be a "liquidity event" imminent? Or is the publisher market different than the marketers'? Read last year's AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV07v8vhgQDcOmngaBtVmycnsBbI3R6oqlTsfpO5dnIT6Dc8oVs0X3o3W_qaGxbJfRxWtdfTLFdnqfr4qCJ2JL2LXSCuREZ2CX4rByacpl1IXuJ5-5G1k5QZQvPk6xMvcmn7rnGuUj3dBp5V_eQW3JK5TAyPBuWX4p5A=> &A with Visual Revenue. 


The Google Policy


Google privacy policies are unifying under a single umbrella policy as Big G is getting closer to the world of an online service provider. As announced on Tuesday, if you want to live in the Google web, you're going to need to ante-up with some PII that allows the company to target you with some sweet ad love. The Google Pubic Policy blog says there are exceptions <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV06CUhn-dZ8dHrrZ-yBbRwgEoZCWvRPAKEyjcH_wfLUp5oQkLAx6ovT-KDMc_3MA1f1LhZ70d3l0KZjgnTsNXJXuEC6Z7pv-fbrqPqQFfuH-pg2wH4g3xlWbFQAEhn6Z8K6hStaNmjALtIp0Q2dxBo3vwcPuR_019aTt4xAkQMvcf4LzUbtxCy72PxPuXUfejcw=> . But, Google is leveraging the need which the consumer has for its tools (search, email, Google docs, now G+) against the consumer's ability to do without. Facebook is the other company with an essential login, of course. Read the policy <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV07l6wGseyBTJN7RwhI78Ewd9V34XTkEHYg-79Eu6FgPntPsmnsHZuxqdl6Fh8i-whbtFsxQWOgzayyWV2-QO5igejE0KYyEmNOkjTjBaWVxIKzBQrkj-LRn> . And, read more in The Washington Post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV05a4p9zywIbbysYYJ2q21HJ3UVCPj6KRPr-7wZe4b57jJiTvYGVHP_7Dy36t317L3mK7eOtcnix3IlxVIdFGmhaSKTkn0xh-Egqp4CNsn2EgeQ3Z5lcgbuZ0A-_SGN71DkTOsExRmwkwcm74nyI34BoWiN7-UyeH1biUoEgRbV2K6AcYP3aNUr59R546JHHghHPKQB9vFQyfCva-qd6ygKHq42xyua-yXGPN2J-An5Hfl9_u2Uy05qyylucgdvCnUU=>  


DSPs In India


Demand-side platforms are infiltrating the media business in India says RP Singh in ClickZ Asia. Singh writes, "The India market is clearly getting divided into brand and performance advertisers. Looking at how SEM is being used in India by advertisers, most performance advertisers have in-house teams to optimize SEM campaigns in real time. These advertisers will continue to handle DSP interface too, in house." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV04aXr8Fzy-CTfsQsVRGtAOS_plOsCYP9paFDh4fuKlrz0L0LMJIsqmm0N2xKvGGVjxzzz2KQ4ax1syi7r9MXq7LsTiMDnN3FU04zwn_vUa2K8Q4ZyERtH8w4uzxWdNN4Z0ZxqHU81hz8DQIW9UekwtJN0kHcUbC_7g=>  


That Sucking Sound Is Your Service 


On his personal blog, Chango CRO Dax Hamman cuts to the chase as he begins his latest post, "What is it with digital marketing? Why are service levels so bad, and why does it seem so wildly accepted? I remember when I was on the agency side and was growing a media team, the flow of sloppy emails, crappy presentations and a whole ton of bullsh*t from vendors and publishers seemed never ending." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV06dTXBA1wg2cFdtbJr2sKJsW_qto572ff5KaYBY5GrPJN9pnZwmmKWh_KezazJoyQlaS1hVFE46aWrPbEhITOKBPizpNGXQIJUGtd53VPETr1QcoPMD3xfXolxKRcTvoFwXD-9k7ssPpQvApQ49hBWy8RLguSJEWzcUwyaL2Xz9Dg==> . Hamman isn't done as he provides some retargeting strategy over on Searchengineland <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV05mTnNxoVvexBQ10YLaL3UOp4VTQjd9QZRzbMf1G0OfFHD0PLUKjJwc6Fev9WUsLToCWcK97iptFpT9iYowxJp1hE9ez7s298nnKmtwyPyIVCeGeD-lWfx5YkXJEC1XvR_FCpNlKAZMd-C0cJZlZhlm49ziln30RLZi0NkDGUhqeKNd-eqm6rZSDMIxdCpPLRQ=> . 


When DSPs Attack


Mike Shields takes a look at demand-side platforms for video on Digiday. This isn't your mother's ad network as Shields writes, "While video ad nets can get away with charging $5 CPMs by layering on lot of low cost, autoplay or in-banner inventory, TubeMogul's prices are in the $10 to $17 range, the more precise a buyer gets. That's cheaper than Hulu, but it's more than some buyers are used to paying for video." Better targeting costs more. Impressions are presumably more qualified. But is there scale? Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV05iQEfE6Vhwc1HX9Z8wYKo6nQAVqJeCAsIpeyWYHc38uo-Pia8jeMWVxWjV2URpEQcw-dlwRxs32QNGEn4MTdfqZn_hyK7WWM8q5vUxNunDJur0rmMZX95XHA7O7PzdvDOMkXfH6JrsULIKqsG6kaDs8hmSQKToPRzfocmqUVvSOw==> .

The Creative Barista


On the Upstream Group blog, Doug Weaver pours a cup of sales "Joe" and challenges sellers to avoid the cheap stuff and keep drinking gourmet. Weaver writes, "Last time I looked, the gourmet coffee business was doing pretty well. The commodity market is what it is. But those who create experiences, identify with a higher calling and properly define their roles and channels almost always transcend commoditization." Sip from the cup of transcendence <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV05Kp6FFzWqi7Y7_6t1y0zZ15NhZzNab9gJbkjNHwCatWRCV78BQXt7L9STzVdTzaYWIfQwO0ZUtQIV1DSbelexLt3E26EPEEtkCB2f7ZcSEp80DsLKoDVw00YUi24uf3TQ=> . 


Retargeting Loves Creative


Retargeting firm AdRoll isn't forgetting creative in its lastest company blog post. Company president Adam Berke gets on his pulpit and exclaims, "Rejoice right-brainers, in 2012 we'll see creative become the focus of new technology and data application. Advertisers should stop milking algorithms for a measly ROI bump of 0.001%, and start caring about the actual content they're displaying." Milk creative says AdRoll <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109156183476&s=8442&e=001kHUGKbfLV04-eeQRiBBGIcP12WRbKaO_iecMw8B1U6qfP8030NPUkds1nVUzBQA0d2RsuiwGZz5S0oveMh5xDP_Xit4BvX4-UHiboc7AFYdvDt8Xa6qxozbQ4nghF8OCLS1QSVkLTX4gv6S4x62MtfvtqQPsUmsCaAlzMKaelSP7eQk-N_jhqc8utR155bmzmjzlzolrWUo=> .

Yahoo! Earnings Revealed


The song remains the same - for now. From Yahoo!'s Q4 earnings release, "Revenue excluding traffic acquisition costs (ex-TAC) was $1,169 million for the fourth quarter of 2011, a 3 percent decrease from the fourth quarter of 2010." And then, the display details: "Display revenue ex-TAC was $546 million, a 4 percent decrease compared to $567 million for the fourth quarter of 2010." Data-driven display is not coming to the rescue here - likely due to a slide in revenue on the "premium"/guaranteed/Class 1 side in "the Americas" where Yahoo! display revenue has been a traditional sweet spot. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109143706767&s=8442&e=001RBmKNDyXioCgLa28jbTUYBxQ6njA0U-TdWGtAJaaZc_3Tq1AvYzuS0WE_i08v7nYyVBeU8hItrnQXdCaWNHVAy-KCevymwbaviaYjHNPJRNtTFL9Zyf0SmCgo2DzV5keB-hZJOwioZ86jY_s94mm2wFnIBCYd0gokVGOk7tIeDQ=> . And, read Jason Del Rey on Ad Age <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109143706767&s=8442&e=001RBmKNDyXioB8hGTvv8-gyCSydJ0x-b374oUWx2qt1nJjPQyCMfdcWBE81pdYcOgtarfl8zZadJhf8MYNxaFA8MT5S1RmoPP_BO-wf_4EaWDglV2NHUhQYYtqSD_ZEKpC5GobFILFaYFu9MkolsygCOYXBFcomvJoF159k0gHANOZ-_bv9JGARR3XTtU1HjC15DWwJhjyg7aHT2qWepshvA==> . In his first appearance on an earnings call, new Yahoo! CEO Scott Thomson was enthusiastic about the company's prospects but said in his intro, "The company has been growing users and launching products at a faster rate, but we need better execution to accelerate time-to-market and to better monetize the engagement we have." Read the transcript on Seeking Alpha <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109143706767&s=8442&e=001RBmKNDyXioBDsjM6g3wHdLXuZpWswnqfzbGYr7qzUQfZOE0uu0l923TwCY0tMPMeWoP-Ykfn3QCw_4yrHUs2BQDfUxLjThKm9kp7YOZ6pyLCIdCBc5NzDs3k-_ySZbpBdokXFDgR4E20leXAE8SiWxCBkQx4LEb2dRLWWRwIq1TCH9s-WkthGvpVF29p420w5wL_u7OJYv4bsxhGqZr9uBvtuzcEAWhN> . Interesting to note that Yahoo! claims interclick benefits/revenues are not readily apparent because now that interclick is internal, it can't record revenue like it used to when it did things such as buying and selling of Yahoo! inventory. At least that was my interpretation of a CFO Tim Morse answer. In general, like his CEO introduction, Thompson was still punting on most strategy questions with only two weeks of experience under his belt. Hear a replay of the call. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109143706767&s=8442&e=001RBmKNDyXioBqQd8TQqMj5C64o__q_g7aVcahid0bjL-EhXP5ZoktkcP5ffaPkLm3bURFXT4a6_Nhe6cxLoUjSdOuyKa_JxFs5PBCAuLCXJS8uXjJn4lYUgYvlj6usLA6>  Citi analyst Mark Mahaney told investors about Yahoo!, "Its core Display Ad biz seems like a Deteriorating Asset - a possibly perpetual market share loser - while its Asia Investment Portfolio would seem to contain significant Shareholder Value creation opportunities. We applaud YHOO's significant share repo activity and would encourage the consideration of a dividend." 


About Closed Systems


Google VP of Product Neal Mohan answers questions from Brian Morrissey on Digiday. Mohan takes exception to the idea that Google is building a closed ecosystem for display just like search: "Anybody who says that and has an understanding of how our industry works knows that is ridiculous. The best way is to give some examples. First of all, when we started in the display business, Google operated a display ad network. Yet we chose to build an ad exchange that was open to all the competitive networks." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109143706767&s=8442&e=001RBmKNDyXioAKkusEVXvSTpcYwEVM2mf8viqERWwawQ1CDav4VNGC8ktquvQOPyFR3he3XFpBNFqLB5s-Jn7j6X556gFtqijVZ6VEWk-4dRtarS4p3AYZvZmIDrrUM8PqG_GT2KhNSL14igCKMf5OUcxhX3P9CBImDVBtqZxr8xGbdg9zerph9HqZAVDFY8ph> . 


More Private Exchanges


In an article on New Media Age, Tim Gentry, Guardian News & Media's commercial effectiveness manager, adds some fuel to the private exchange fire and says that, hey, it works! Rubicon Project's private exchange offering is highlighted as Gentry says, "Ensuring that we're capturing more of the spend in the market from trading desks like Vivaki's Audience on Demand & Group M's Xaxis, our share of the Rubicon [Project] UK News Channel grew from 11% to 18%, growing our effective cost per thousand impressions (eCPM)." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109143706767&s=8442&e=001RBmKNDyXioC3EGTnQCnHMwBd66Hl-eNjqj3aRn5Z3o-xoFlaUMPvRki1Y74aFvIjyhBcbpnRByHfCgPfXTorSBL_7V_YRNKl9Pz8WTdROlT_Z-tJCI8HP827FCzYxuaV-CpAnV3sG_-ZeUD8d7uFocIrwWTPVtGaQSEmmmjv5ptd8kg7r-fr0Hha6CnjHq1__9M3XrMXPJWpU4gd7d8d1IayoAgsIzCU> . 


Microsoft And VivaKi


More video to view! Publicis' VivaKi Nerve Center CEO Curt Hecht speaks to the Microsoft Ad crew at the recent Consumer Electronics Show in Las Vegas. Hecht sees opportunities for VivaKi in several areas in the coming year with Microsoft. He notes Xbox and, on a test-and-learn basis for VivaKi, Skype. He says the Microsoft Exchange represents an important part of the exchange-driven, audience-buying-driven marketplace. He also hopes to see more competition internationally being provided by Bing. See it (gonna need Silverlight to view it) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109143706767&s=8442&e=001RBmKNDyXioDZiOJH3nFWO3JQr2GL-SnMY_C7MyicetQ28xsJwK7XFkUv9YCnmX7Uw2wVLcs7ZzFEPLDYtkHHfNU8FmLK1HponUweBQspJCWIjhDEQSUsnCBMH3drEYQ-_xXfW2rAGhCkdkbM1WhhhKlNk8uQDOEVrKODvUpVH3pyohOZ0CGLa3y6LGhuXXBfj2SyUCJbCzgP9J-pi9BtvVJHjBcWnCUcN7yp_rm5AzpXkaW1fbOFncCYRfZPp_HMpi1MWQiIogvLETVHAYwUz11FZ5wg7yqwJqmVUSM5VuU=> . 


Getting Netezza'd


For a while there, you couldn't enter the demand-side platform tech conversation if you didn't have a pricey Netezza computer helping you with the number crunching - and a press release announcing the "box", too! Netezza has since been acquired by IBM and is now focused on an even more global mission. Following up last week's National Retail Federation show, and similar to the rest of "Smarter Commerce" IBM, the Netezza unit is now squarely aiming at CMOs and their CIO friends as it "announced a new analytics appliance that analyzes up to petabytes of big data including consumer sales data and online shopping trends to help retailers gain actionable insight on buying patterns." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109143706767&s=8442&e=001RBmKNDyXioD7_S2hNUDDk-R0SoS3yOsP37elymE-bWPzcGUfjqiuyyECRR9kz-dOSOCB1bsqRF60S3Idtwy2ZJbBIXBAJsDO5deOc6dYo-BsWwP8dZOkSOgaD9HYZWmqXYeACFlwc1P-1O2TjOMmM7Uu_2XodKoyY4faw1JHGp4PE7eCuU2EFvql-8I2DB_yzC63E6uYh4yLyuNV6WUjlltajujXNM3lkv5jvT9ncAiuL-EZ9x67XQ==>

Apple Teller Machine 

Apple made enough money in the fourth quarter to buy the startup ad tech ecosystem and ad holding company or two. From the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoErrOxH1xYQS7W2KhmfiBG6mKSad4OFBaeerHTfr08SPgYNl1htw-li-_K_3I558Rbl_NBtQX8IUEcSXoJDrN6h_1iMQzk9yHYdsGz9Er4iB-l_8dvtPeRe72vEn4GQ7llfrBVhuIKZYLffSMW3cuvmnSu-pWtVNyTv_3esjwvW1txryimn_5rOHtpodxhILjuU=> , "The Company posted record quarterly revenue of $46.33 billion and record quarterly net profit of $13.06 billion, or $13.87 per diluted share." Analysts had thought Apple would make $10.06 per share on revenue of $39 billion according to CNET. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoEqpwaYzEmHFGk1g5x77I1ZDAhHJIiun09t8QKFLCu86spYZfEdRcQ8klxYsVCBICxDWBVMBC4gi5McBgLxcFS6vU7S4C5oJcLSAll866-UVZ3uIsCOBQItZyYrdxbHHHNmg2ezYmvYNV9GBpj9yPnj93tZmARYIanSgrGtt-yZvyjhP7BhQxkg0jfVpXguebTvXm2LSIdIgyA==>  iPhone was Apple's Q4 killer app. 


Another Acquisition


More ad tech company acquisitions! - or mergers to be exact. Shopper marketing company DiJiPOP (AdExchanger.com Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoEqUHYtB1ZHFm9taZjgoTHGNV7wCo4Wp9BxV8cJx874c0QzwAY6M137mRsrbCqd_Widj9EQVeLSBtTAEFZDSSXDGXMkl_Ahn_OavWuzqV0L_c-PWFfh3KsnKAff3mysg_t4-baX4ERfK_w==> &A) has been acquired by ownership targeting company OwnerIQ. Also, OwnerIQ let a few details go in the press release as it says its "revenue has nearly quadrupled in the past year, as agencies have made increasing use of the company's ability to reach consumers based on ownership signals." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoEoYKkgysXFBlRMMkrRwuOezDLRLYfM9DLMi9t_Kuvt8itutcbs_3_M81aN66c-urZrN9wIPlUwrzpsk4nqDjd-95i7xJXjBMF-9_EUw_vslWb65MWFBP-Ra-8LHUmqEpLrWDDCkdT8I2A==>  


Looking At LUMA


On the Perfect Market blog, and in Powerpoint format, CEO Julie Schoenfeld offers "a simplified version of the LUMAscape (online ad ecosystem map) by focusing on the 6 major functions involved in the display ad value chain." And there are no logos! See it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoEq8iVDoWufAxuJW5q0cjpZun--6ZLyb-GyGe0xP2vu_QUVur6mS80vDYVAXSQj1_47d1IrmdC0krOGuyjMVZCYVfiAQDHE1X0hhF9A884um-plyQ2SGFC0RuCEQrPfJGSrYsJK7xm0w_nkAznCB1ojkS0SxYBHnFsM=>  Schoenfeld sees "drastic" changes ahead for the ecosystem. 


AllCash


In the New York Post, Keith Kelly reports that Meredith is expanding its food footprint as it has acquired AllRecipes.com for $175 million from Reader's Digest Association. Kelly writes, "The site, which was modestly profitable on revenues of just under $30 million a year, drew 25.4 million unique visitors in December, according to comScore. That was a whopping 5 million more than No. 2 site Foodnetwork.com, which had 19.7 million visitors." Let the CPG ad dollars flow. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoEqRivr7kvmtjjrEsJnG5nFPIkH-6m5UtCLl6CdQoolUa8-6YFm4RYBRnfUnfvMfNEE8pm1myR6f6X--OyHHublLtsOyGj1L1EAfksI6x7EPT2waIdvAyRJrFZlEMLZLvSSSunGRIiRotaMbsYpE9IRT_ETGO951BZTy2-NhHH96RnhgJX5Bg6txIzLcd4R7-B0UZOMrkfdN9A==> . 


Still More For Retail


Loyalty audience platform, Adara Media, announced that it has taken in over $12 million in new funding to drive growth. CEO Layton Han (AdExchanger.com Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoErJNd7XWQeWg7f877EQdKBW2vwaXNEynhxR4ND1OF582zL_LBb0H_pkSIzp8qT5i1nU5gqqzfR1zrXrBInFATv4Itkh5c5eszHQhQ91Mc7hSjz0_J1cONW2R4v7gpIIOGqwuIUvhfcV09v5r7syazq3bbLOAX6L9__CWoNQHb_ileUXM7bPCng5LSvs4LYZmT8iLIHUazMxfidZ6ZTcS6m-iLfYAuq4Fyi3fJpgEkrTBDodAm-9s4WmQNhbNNwvXLg=> &A) said in the release that, in part, his company will "use the funding to take the TruPrecision platform into new vertical categories. The company's growth in 2011 has come from travel, hospitality and closely related verticals." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoEq3ZK5BUNoZA23vcWjP5Up7sQ7PmqsrI2UQqa0nv6VSQhqAQ3gK__qbNjR-GhzjG_BvZFPTyUn4PNTwG9jBSoEiC4UXMhnWOJtvSI5qtOOJvL5IcOdLN_y4y2z8Yb-lVkiNYKqzGXst3aWqRTXVjtQ_haMX6zD-UDuaJEe7sMa6eWhb2SsxJgDXw3EBAQ_-Lcpuhp_Z21R5EhRCBPV_3480Bjrc5aBI_fw=> .

Verifying Video Ads


Digiday's Mike Shields discusses the ad verification business with AdSafe Media and its CEO Scott Knoll. Shields inquires about AdSafe's video ad verification product to which AdSafe's Knoll responds, "We have a bunch of video-network clients. So that says something. But the reality is, we've had mixed results trying to look at the video itself and trying to figure out if something is appropriate [content/context-wise]. We've done all kinds of testing, looking at meta tages, pages, keywords words. We found that 99 percent of the time there is a correlation between a video's content and other info we pull from the page it appears on."
Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoEpLlOAWFV7vN2cDm9mpwEDC_asVAsShockr61Rt5zWFElWsY_tTIJG1tEqxiy9e5urD4g6Yokfsc_eRdV_Qq2R6aZHQi_bz31UuiivKObCvDDvO6LT_OoMcSEpXUMNpbJqWKJPqTDQu1O044jQ9jZI4> 


"Dow Jones" Intent Index


Twelvefold Media (formerly BuzzLogic) announced its new "Mindset Index" where the idea is to pull in all those unstructured bits of data on you and me and turn them into insights on intent such as "looking to shop," "deal seeker," "expert advice seeker" or "loves AdExchanger."
Read the Twelvefold blog post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoEpPkoXxu_7Knm32MgEsEepIedB63M1DVNa1UxXr6WDAzDNya88NS8myBfUspOub1-SuFOAzEN-twDJAlbj55CmHYO9uHcS34JMYrr9mnlHm7_PbyexIEpPWFEjWVvOuGnBkoEBEFZhImksizscvelD_hpFqQ1uQoMob-gsgRwQmTPHQ7tfbL8Hm-9a_XxYVVbiirJCIs3cIEH4dxB7U9knjID_n0VLfn6Je7ytGG-Pk0A==> 


Give Me Malware.. Protection!


Twitter appears to be taking proactive on protecting its own ad tech strategy by acquiring a company called Dasient in order to beat back the scourge of the data-driven world: malware! Wired's Mike Isaac writes, "Dasient is a leader in the prevention of 'malvertising,' the practice of incorporating malicious code and links to harmful sites into ad content. The ruse is similar to the standard hacker technique of luring an unsuspecting web surfer into clicking on a malicious link." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoEq2OXH8eaPQM53URb8Z1nRJpnbenoeycv_gExSX8hKKj6TgHf5pNtsjxz9Eqf21_ssa8aRoTamlmyI5vjzO-C0VWCwwEOS1zG1dsCIuJO9HVAwMrggIjmD3mNr_S5CcXJMHT9e2syNZMvkmLkEJmVraNm1pwp1-N0kOqCsaDVJLAQwbijroPCe4> 


And The Results Are In


Yahoo! Q4 2011 earnings are coming your way on Thursday after the market's close.  Get 'em here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109131334103&s=8442&e=001d6U0eH8RoErcA4Z6YIh8CS2nPpN3OD5URLW6HMOLmOxeI5MwYDG0ndU4dDI2SWdmcvPY2Ys9JaxG3cIELdA75IQ41kmPJhh_zYhf8f0xu5WXHMx8OyCommI0JPBzUS6P> . Citi's Mark Mahaney suggests what to watch for in a note to investors: "1) New CEO Scott Thompson's early commentary; 2) any discussion on strategic alternatives-we continue to think an Asian asset cash-rich split would be the best option if Yahoo! is not able to sell the entire company; 3) color on headcount and costs given recent reports that a hiring freeze and workforce reduction may be coming (AllThingsD); 4) signs of sales force traction in display; and 5) signs of RPS improvements."

Adjusting The Audience Algo


If you want to target high net worth audiences, you may want to set your latest algo to target the tablet device. New data from Pew Research points to a quickly growing and potentially cash-rich demo if you compare tablet ownership before and after the holidays. Pew says: "More than a third of those living in households earning more than $75,000 (36%) now own a tablet computer. And almost a third of those with college educations or higher (31%) own the devices. Additionally, those under age 50 saw a particularly significant leap in tablet ownership." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109124259988&s=8442&e=001jENVFa6MMsTX1osRLGsz25Iz56N78Vo4YYubksa5UJJl43HAuLXd-rDhCJMAjql8uUfX_VSao0hbAvbguw7cojFeLDv9Z1Cv5bgzUnblwLOf8CjClac1Yawgz6DVjoDnJ1SLHGmq-0rmZv3cpLuKVNMxYnfezw1LUbTZcTVhSzOeLC4EQqZzL80RMR_n0in2bS54-KwzSj4=> . Meanwhile, Starcom's Mark Pavia says there's big creative potential in the tablet on MediaPost <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109124259988&s=8442&e=001jENVFa6MMsRvH_w0hOlU55ovE2AZ6mlZWrBP7ufIDdd00mJPLEjruHDT3F8iEf3bts1bDRtdTDbtt_z9R1mwI3_9EjU8MqXLMlSAlboS-BgkxSqbASzPbvo4VngBYzHusqbtPCdEAG7U2lgfEImiJf-y8_3L_0SYsxJI6YZWJamu7hB2ftXTUj9Kr5DkHfXB3hO4HzZ-gFeuU90bb8R77A==> . 


Ad Network Lab


India-based ad network Komli Media announced that its starting a research unit for online ads, Komli Labs. According to VC Circle, "The digital media lab, which will be located out of the company's Bangalore-based R&D centre will focus on online advertising optimisation, trends, audience targeting, real-time bidding and traffic quality management." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109124259988&s=8442&e=001jENVFa6MMsT7-VAz8OqDpLDGXsFrfSvTrLHyggxpRZ5z4gkwOsoPVl0_Ora_v_DZ2E4d9gyND5mG3bAaqQ8YfyrhCjR61ZY6LZ8VaQ2QEzpt0Sjmg0HLY2TDgd8Q71MyDTqLL1Q2Y_BkHRB12tN68P32dKGbQ4upe9GK1jbEnbBciRXS2VMimTOSzwJWbYhtfxjH0LEpnQ4=> . 


Data Drives The Agency


New MEC North America chief Marla Koplowitz provides a look at her CEO role in an interview in Adweek. Regarding the future of media agencies, she doesn't hesitate to grab the data-driven dynamite: "One of the areas you are starting to see media agencies go toward is data - data and analytics and more accountability in terms of what media agencies can deliver. The ability that we now have is to really start measuring the experience. That is where we can really start to push as an agency and start to link back to the strategies that we're developing..." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109124259988&s=8442&e=001jENVFa6MMsTztQCYV0tCT7O7wXPCr-6byrpiyAI2R6Y4xtCWdUwyS4MGyG4O3BhF81RElpnzjuoQYSpdDvQ7sv2ta9S7hoi8fLS5zitKTRCIPZ7DNYGCFsjAqYCIwYIcg6Zv_uSvqy_OW_yuipzJBOdRHyCQYL_l4G7oouPmm-6Y6RKoKfD2mQdeacLygQU2wh9H1g8nzVI=> .

Big! Data!


Media buying and data management platform Turn lets two of its employees loose on ClickZ to provide an example of big data in action. Turn's Mael Bredeche, Chris Kane point to something called "Site Extension" to explain the actionable insights available in BIG! DATA! in online ads. They write, "At the most basic level, the concept of site extension is to identify a custom network of sites whose visitor populations are very similar. If a campaign is successful on one site in the network, that performance can then be extended across the other similar sites. The solution requires two key ingredients - a massive data warehouse..." ...and Jolt Cola? Taste the other ingredient. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109124259988&s=8442&e=001jENVFa6MMsTNpYrKK39NxZSJSQyDcGpRLq85us4hFm888dzzgax4qqNoNQl6jIjR7MGGmHCuRMUfnapbYk29vcInIUktC3EH2ajCmLQ_D5Zj516GbaEbRPJc5ULTRv0XmCTmP0DHiuoPLDnxycwwWbr9x6VLq0k2kVHv7naUU-pKnNcGwkGnmQ==>  


Bidding From The Trough


On ExchangeWire, display ad specialist firm Infectious Media's Martin Kelly says that real-time bidding (RTB) has hit the "trough of disillusionment" for the advertiser. Kelly explains, "Current benefits of RTB to an advertiser are pretty scant. Centralisation and control of retargeting, along with black box optimisation algorithms are as far as anyone can get, and are all trading and workflow related benefits." Read what he thinks is needed <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109124259988&s=8442&e=001jENVFa6MMsTmZYldxrii7aWxahkXKjrgdKaAuL2FXj6RQ9PgAJSTNdahO8A2aG1uAu_PVs5nG-3qKGzeWwc0fe_H3igqaXPcbMv6LGlikMwwt9m908rokNEjTnZRzzf6-AdCjfy6iM7QeJbEUhFCvSHhfUkffvCSCoA-V_za4qeuFyI5AzE-QR7juMEkmekrwcN7-wpdmUI=> . 


The Straz Remedy


Numerous unfilled positions and high turnover rates expose the talent crisis within advertising agencies. Matt Straz diagnoses the problem in a fourfold solution that is likely the core of his new company Namely. He recommends that companies focus their energy towards incorporating more outreach, technology, training and diversity within their policies. Read more on MediaPost. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109124259988&s=8442&e=001jENVFa6MMsQAnOVRUgyxFgJxoKzqnbvTwKqNvKKT9EKMD4X6JzHRb-E7nYD0w6iF2A9cdHJk2gCpLKb5PrOc73ZJpGnBba9uuSXWZspFcMjmlympYK29QJNRTGGprrwB6LPQ0T6kXcIZ5Hn2AWJpJKpDRYkKkgiYryNeQjCWlPMyPCun6_ynAcM3LjtYx5dYDwBFc3DvuSoKwWzQRF_LGw==>

Targeting Showrooming


Identifying yet another digitally-inspired buzzphrase - "showrooming" - The Wall Street Journal reports that mega-retailer Target has had enough of being the brick-and-mortar showroom for online retailers and its telling its vendors to either create products uniquely delivered to Target that better differentiate from competitors - OR make an effort to meet the lower prices offered elsewhere. Read it (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCBSM4i2Pzy-WPLRGFKKAI_VViM3M8oiOyl4s0kBTqWaBWFsUMOtZ1Y1sL3xTzXdSmazDLFfqb-84r4tGzKq8YFnchfst_g3W5z12iWwUoRn2GVeC7gaX95fqdY8bgBmpwSP4q3kgktHbx93CfQ9D32wHgqszi7UY4_LZRRgitbTaB1_VEazPp2y> . Analyts are dubious this work for certain commoditized products given the cheaper labor costs through the online-only model. 


Reviewing Email Vendors


The "Waves" keep crashing ashore at Forrester Research as the latest Wave report takes a look <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCC65If15XqC8TOLhtUsuHzhKdZC5oM7UXKCHBncYxU3nivOaq-RQIicUn_rS0jAeGFa99TAa-SYQLR5d14M09moqQsrcIy4-rlErgiOwNOlkSV3wgh2JWMx3VrkH1w4LqHDi133l3GmhF6u8yrqHOtHocEp7mL3oYXRsThUsaH0iCgEucFAbCTO5HCHaa3ktT3vLuc7nD7B7WsQrvmF2yrcUlFFpzxGJjEX-IDfD0Yjbj3Zg9W3UCBo3JoAXf9mBVp9JB933o3tdwofBjljcNPqvusR8D0D91w4BL-750c0rMHgAHZD7UvH>  at email marketing vendors. Following their DSP <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCD_BI-ozZKjpb7AxO4ZxT7ndCMQdqoSoepgAvLI_9_rH4-p5AnmXaY3FtLaM1hymf7Sz0lWX6JVxNIts7G4tIe9wUTdBSoqUJmOXbkFwpZSMQUhomrN3trR5PmsTKJkS-10tYTSymgDXSab2yXunS_aTyFupyGKIPU=>  and SSP <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCADOK2X0E-WohNeXOFaBlYqht6fRdB6OpkmBjhnDOI9VK9_HJL3MWoRPobWTPCYall2o7u5ioIcV_w9AksFuJJv66M47zU5HLN3mLMy1khXdtSVIgDivYZB61dV-xThAjpvqGykjO85nVvQwwDHz4TYIAzQthmoYQ4=>  Waves, a Forrester team of authors led by Shar VanBoskirk chose 6 out of a possible 48 vendors to review including Epsilon, ExactTarget, Experian CheetahMail, Responsys, StrongMail and Yesmail Interactive. Get the free download from Responsys (pay with some PII) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCAi9ZC83dJt9ybnvcCiDMRxsZSFCGAGXkXA8l1NQ3hyUrtRxAPgWdFLgRUyn9P1CtuErN1GWQNM58_Npk7Dz48lGpMxi-9UPfvkVbOoWVaN7_G5RvKgVIGr1GEXS_-Mqq--6GVYmGV68uNAgyJPGXtz> . Responsys and ExactTarget rated the best according to Forrerster. Strongmail and Yesmail were at the back of the pack. Forrester notes that most of the cross-functional marketing service providers (MSPs!) like Acxiom are slowly retiring or stopping investment in email marketing platforms and leaving it to "independent, technology-led firms" to take the lead. 


Dallaire Leaves, Katz Takes Lead Sales Role


Seth Dallaire is returning to Amazon as its VP of North America sales according to Kara Swisher of All Things D. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCAK3j76yNCfakY3-liatR1n1_V-1WbipU5JmrkMlUF4KIrOCZboPwsuPEQmR3sbx83acZzSzPA6U2H4PaHUvPoc5J1KfN9uMU03RzFYGhxfkvvav_17EFRsXzSwVawQavnpImruWv7BAxoaAjQFpucUseCXo_f5usLjn7Akrr2CJw==> . According to his LinkedIn profile <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCA3_98yHqXHHNz11bM4SdfHegfM470T3RGMsLk-A1hf39rLisJFjdccls4ThGBIip1FWT0P-Sk22CvEbtlZgLKt7zRw_0hVr5OVimJyWO5CYWejPUn-tbXHCj-fZv9p8hQzgKGFPAcrLVJ8mncrQakz> , Dallaire was "Sr. Account Manager - Business Development" back in 2002. Dallaire (AdExchanger.com Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCB6NwT-_VgTN8bvHkdCMK08L2DzpTCbwzWL6YBxeroaufscnSBO9xBt0Dym_IRIY54kkA2e24S0JnagfmBmCTdunHU0qsY2T6FJbfKSCPr2_ahslpOdPKVcrwYVd3WYXk_amDob-BX5hOqhsxtts3KZ5rr6Ce1J7Fg=> &A in Aug. '11) was a key cog in efforts to create better relations with the agency world. On Friday, Swisher reported on next steps in a Yahoo! sales re-org and quoted a Yahoo! internal memo attributed to Wayne Powers saying that, among other moves, interclick CEO Michael Katz "will lead all sales operations and data and performance optimization for the combined [interclick and Yahoo! mid market sales] teams." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCBm08fUuUCvZ_S4bBoiICaB5405WSNQnAETL1L7wgEP2Pcgj-XScGPZldxzVf52UyGV1mYJShaZH_nO-kW-b6oBbC8JcgxDDjHYyfOeHwUuLG8V-PnZaJY2q538kH-comtUlz8QQgIpGHkLqStVs7KOnJGRUIZut4h_rMyMuA_2-GCzUQdtyisLsWXLD_dltpm0kaZ79hm9txagGjmFNRiY>  


Do-Not-Track In The EU


European Commission VP Neelie Kros says she supports a 'do not track' (DNT) standard, and not just for the EU but the world over. She writes on her European Commission blog, "A global DNT standard would describe the technical details of a 'signal' that users can send, to providers, via their online equipment, including their web browser." She points out this standard isn't just about stopping tracking if the user wants to do so. It's also about providing more personalized advertising. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCDr1PSLrZH2p6nxnm6XF9c5DjCB6yuflxg7reSmpTokwAiz3GznP1EnuMcTHvsYZwHAQYnfRtvO2M09yF_Hz32DUt1IFZW-m8BGsztjYhauUaWw87ccTOLN_-MxgzLCM7MNQF_iujkjRwyRPPQYvFZu>  


Pumping Up The Icon


The Digital Advertising Alliance (DAA), who helped guide the online behavioral advertising/privacy icon development as well as ongoing management of its rules and regs, is undertaking an ad campaign of its own to educate consumers. According to the release, the "'Your AdChoices' public education campaign designed to inform consumers about interest-based advertising and how to take greater control of their online privacy." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCDBPMD4Mb9s8F7hvL97nV2kDe3Zr6A_v0QdPYac3qeHJiku0Kp4mHqqxJnZBH1xZWb48Pm4kB9usfyaZq8rBsSnK0N03Llry6IQZvnow_dHL2BPRxLf2cHYZAXP0SY7fE8mevMWOT_QAf1XItaX7SDJETGwqaiJJwLQc1lQ3mJxRSuLTTi1giUAxsUEt5haaGyjUJ3dU7Ciu1TpuMYcJddsBUfcVapRktiHLL6EHCdkoP0n41y1m-MUhbGOE7szAfuSiGJwK_UA9w==>  Ad Age highlights a few examples <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCAPBTFUutKZydTOzYnY-_IWRbhpYs6TkfhTkiiCDWbVV5l6kP5QNLXsQXEDCRIkzA1MUwDGc-_ae7EnuBuetc2_EakmHBrKIN95Ayk8471TNQk0KFxnSddHbjgNuouI_-PUSj3V0b98XmBPtMpdussj6gufmEUtP2jAfjtw0_OFoze-2kw08hcC96WD6IIZ93I2rUUsXZoV_QaR_Zt11dGO>  of the campaign and asks readers, "This new campaign frames the debate over targeting in a more positive light than past efforts, but (...) Will this be effective in changing the public perception of targeted ads?" Unless there's millions of dollars behind this - with online and TV ad spend - the best effort would seem to be ongoing self-regulation efforts in concert with industry education of regulatory agencies which will disseminate opinion to politicians and consumers. 


Math Men And ATDs


Redpoint Ventures VC Chris Moore runs with the "Mad Men" and "Math Men" metaphors in an opinion piece on All Things D. In the course of making the case for the increasingly data-driven world of advertising, Moore identifies agency trading desks (ATDs) are identified as a sign of the times, "In the last few years, the ad agency holding companies have rolled out their own technology-driven digital ad 'trading desks' to help their clients take advantage of these ad trading platforms. I wonder if they've replaced the scotch in the mini bars with the Math Men's drink of choice, Red Bull." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCB6mZ-sHRtNPBMHcyU1OZxc_J4ec1EMY_Gm5_WrKKQnDekOnkSR0nJ1Z055c2peK76fPYfObWMvEc7A2bVmmwx78kLHH4SoqwK0opXk5BBtGPa1s0tQUZIuphm2DmMkVmSVDbzKlh6urikvJ_hhBzrUXUZmHftWljU7O1uXs11px8JAKn0ZmrHt3uL8V5mY8sY=>  


Clarifying Ad Spend


On ReadWriteWeb, reporter Jon Mitchell pulls from some comScore/AdXpose data and writes, "U.S. advertisers spend nearly $40 billion a year for online advertisements, but 31% of their ads are never seen. That means $12.4 billion will be wasted on U.S. online ads this year." AppNexus CTO Mike Nolet responds decisively in the comments, "Good job writing a wonderfully dramatic post that is naive and wrong. Online advertisers measure their results well and will average *down* the price based on lack of visibility." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCAqHcXNyfFdvNbrSwswx9WN6-t-yhVynSIGrPHIVVcsBVCD7kBfggEIPhwUW--_1Jjff9fnaGB_e68dkWMHPP62SGrtEfWF9iwqPgA8nVOJkbJjKsj-Ig5XwzOimbBgMgKnKRpr1baqO1mFIyML4-y7V_cDwaTZfnSpflP_hB_PDbKAPPkVEzN0LXiBLe-sWbM=> . 


Product Does Marketing


If your company is depending on Microsoft marketing spend in the coming year, you may want to make sure your contacts in the various product groups are strong. Ad Age's Kunur Patel says a reorganization of the marketing function at Microsoft "indicates a larger trend in which product people, often engineers, are wielding more clout in -- and even rising to the top of -- divisions. For example, in December, engineer Terry Myerson took over as the head of the Windows Phone division and will oversee all its marketing." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCDeiq5_ghU_bVhxyaXxDWi2qWqf6wJQPQ6YB_sg8s65bYU_G5_cWo2UUcJ5r8-V-CmcQptg2hwSRU-f7u3R9PYG5T5s13RXQrOXKfeNnaOATOSQDJNOaZ4wqn4XqeroMSSTp_XJC4Oa3VZm5_gJvdxIpkPnGCpkvR0e_VCXbF2N35bVomtIJOw5ZSlmGqEVJYKvuuez191m-g==> . 


Google+ Assimilation, WiFi Targeting


Google+ is now an integrated part of signing up for any Google Account says blog Google Operating System. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCAPDbj-423VwAGECm0bj_hfQQh0DGqJwiOHUPCMrieGH6br6LwXB_TXyAgUBCdezug9prh0t8Iby1zGD6vL7RZSZqIp8EEpFRuWAiJ52wwk-XJBtqMes7FO4UJcXlgT1cNuQib2cbJcQc9g-YjMXJW4OtIlqRZ1myqFExx5S9pizPcQXU9KcPvLu7zIgg9B4G8=>  Google is hellbent on making sure Google+ interest or sentiment-based data is informing targeting and personalization through Google ads, products and services in the future. Meanwhile, on the Google Mobile Ads blog, product manager Morgan Hallmon announced that AdWords advertisers can now target whether a user is connecting via Wi-Fi and by mobile OS. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109113179207&s=8442&e=001lXPkl-XoGCD5wVEaA7Hm_90KrWTMQLXwHfamVlRU2AV_KAj3faY4LtG2zPXQoq7l4_ZUFBvYuUHeaBySEuMfiiCL4TRE5A_Pa59n4RJ-nMBbw8kNzpoR0KUwh-olt-9Ne2jkHwVKwmX4JsmFRPnTTHwUF4jSHM8VChA18jKlmGQ97ci0n-VNHl3QmxT40cKes-lipcvR8Vw=> . Hallmon says the WiFi targeting is "useful if your campaign or landing page has high bandwidth content, like videos that you'd like mobile users to access." WiFi is presumably higher bandwidth than a wireless carrier.

Vibrant Acquires Ad Network


Yesterday, contextual ad network and technology company Vibrant Media announced the acquisition of in-image ad network Image Space Media (ISM). Long-rumored as a candidate for an IPO, Vibrant Media appears to be extending its case for the importance in online advertising of placement and context. From the release, "The acquisition of ISM will enhance the delivery of Vibrant Image, a product that identifies static images within brand-safe content across the Web and embeds small overlays within them at the bottom of the image." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk1q-iHIejOwg5d9azXQ-0qF8IYeskUXElrL9aksl8wcRbZLj6klvUUinCF1Ys0Q3Sw17Plh2Ag228PwDIa88MUyUzd2ywBI7UyiXyr_0s2CpHiA2LZfN6AVoAx_B9gCvEjJHbd76prBNOnFIWI7J2tkS_8JX0wBfLqnrrb4QF9zNe7pnjFMeHJE> . ISM had raised around $3 million according to CrunchBase <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk3HnKDQxXVfgBeLl2r1orTr_pBVR4ROEI2tse7sbrAv0zkhaAkra_WnSU13_71os0XFnMYENQsAp9lq3W75HmstPEi5kvHPddz4fMThSaCHXMqHuGqb-B_gLnFhOTXcZGtf3qPjLbuE5w==> . Was ISM another victim of audience-based buying? Yet, Vibrant powers on. 


Google Display, Aegis ATD 


In The Wall Street Journal, Amir Efrati reviews Google's surge into the world of display advertising and provides an anecdote on just how aggressive Google has been with agencies and their trading desk initiatives such as Aegis' iProspect which helps guide Aegis ATD initiatves. Efrati writes, "Google assigned an employee to iProspect's Boston office. (...) Another Google worker set up shop inside iProspect's San Francisco office a year ago, working there at least twice a week, he added." Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk1dl6Dt_HwsFCbusP0cgC4w6Bj4FNXE1FgZbOKMNY6X548PkyaspfO30OcnxAhfoLIMp8LIHVcPvPSsy5AXFuHUzrnpZ7DMubgpia_9ejqhH9dKOGjMzISGzSP7QCvtWCvjZHbY5Jw3YiFfENK4myhH8o2OpEB0mLE_4yKtFEkhDHFisDoupmoN> . Also, AMNET is the name for the Aegis ATD which according to this job <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk364_N63m6eaG2lRiY4vkgkHtqtACPn4cdVkGEEu1TmJHS3tQptypxUwXV9zPdh2FSLJH99yP4LNu5xxa1n0AeAQ2Z_Z3gNAb2475ubdeFtoWegWeME0d4U5uXdzQfH1hoCCOjDcYgLu9Rv0rH7pKSF86LE4wZY7fDwwUZFdyJ1jw==>  on the AdExchanger.com job board is beginning to crank up in the U.S. View the LinkedIn Group, too <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk0RIPEEPC7ib257TPDkxYrFEB_9UeWpPUeC9DDWjd9zO0R08G2WDfvn9ebHHSO9rMGGs1aXoUk8EfDWBe7ZfrIYFba1_l6HfThQaZ--YVm0__vKgKVpLNfBN5fYEgJwLbVKsYM8vuTLdQDYykDHIhuNhf1y9Fm_7CM=> ... you know you want to. 
 
Retarget Tablets Now!


Adobe has released a new study which it says shows tablet visitors (i.e. iPad users) "spent more per purchase than visitors using smartphones or traditional desktops and laptops, suggesting that tablet visitors were the most valuable online customers in 2011." Tablet-ers spent 54% more than other device channels says Adobe.... Are you segmenting your audience according to device? If you're a publisher, you're fattening those tablet CPMs ASAP - if you have scale that makes it worth it. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk3em0QINpD_1Dev1qKowa2jI-KXsxR2sAhtGwJGuZQOW2Sxk87b0EcQr3KH4bKPAcIzAjyFnLRvNzJq2p1B5wiL1tXIjI7ZEd8BWxoDtrK9B_sseNMODSxsfFwDM2VdJB5ht7adTMbS-qbKYoxFgt0GMpgTNcxkBcWhnJIDlW2Iz2bPJ1JJOfXMjmwHxBf77EfOix3qlUU9u8sQN8UOgQFAy4J8mVj8Pd0=>  And, download the study's findings <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk2kdxTb8TcTROLRzees2zxvp83lrk1S86WbD3C3ijdBy6P92MQf9EW7yRvcWb1w_c4JCesOgwzjFMyZQam01_Y7s5h3MfqzZceAUySyPUkHagg7lF9BskfRnqMb_5UU23HsEBIv-2GWo_ajjvZOT9wJ3oj-PtG3eCdoXrKeIv7XO1S0N1ocEbxpgKCiB0kr7kNDHX81dfVgPQ==> . The "lean back" world of the tablet is more prone to shopping. 


For Your PowerPoint


eMarketer has issued its latest predictions for online ad spend over the next few years. The keyword is "Billions," according to eMarketer. From the press release: "US online advertising spending, which grew 23% to $32.03 billion in 2011, is expected to grow an additional 23.3% to $39.5 billion this year-pushing it ahead of total spending on print newspapers and magazines." Get the graphic for 2012 and beyond <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk18nkIT4rVrkFwPeG0KpmcXZ9RRJx75eoHkrj9JXgZsQhrCERG3fAKQIWYFNZIXibDdcUuAazi-yFMTKORE7MWnKHSwmkOMFnZSuRKwg9_v-7sL2Gf5IFx-HeVnGmnF7i3bKINXBazMyQ01j4RFXXrM> . 


Agencies And The DSP In China


China-based ad platform AdChina and its VP of Marketing, Jing Pan, offers up its "2012 Digital Media Scene Report" in the hopes of providing some insight to its clients (and potential clients) on the opportunity in the Chinese market as well AdChina's own offering. Led by former Ebay-er Alan Yan, AdChina claims to be active in the agency holding company world when it comes to DSP services. From the report: "4 of the top 6 international 4As media agencies in China adopted AdChina DSP to manage their advertising operations in the past 2 years. We estimate significant growth in China's DSP business in 2012." Download it (PPT, 6.5 MB) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk2vOSMqTe7B0GQ3PrQZO6vYsYHbY_xVrpOjIiEOS54mDr9-BN4xw0BgP3awptsNwLUITVURMnJrAmxRP4bPirQCYraG5wkZB4HZuRe4Fk25wUqmmORlGV_icVBfR-cl0eaMauz_8GsKjSCaayyFaw64YO1s-6YsIxSEy5H5IlvuCDctPICUPfZ6WIzNBh_2WT9pEngHXuqxeX1iHi9HXo3T> . Sales pitch aside, if you're looking for aggregated stats for online advertising in Chinese market, the deck is worth a look. 


Verify This


Digiday's Mike Shields looks at comScore's announcement of its vGRP product and the integration of AdXpose. In speaking with comScore CEO Magid Abraham, Shields sees more, "...under the surface, it seemed clear that ComScore is looking to shove aside verification companies like DoubleVerify, view monitoring startups like RealVu, tag management vendors like Tagman and perhaps even brand-researcher firms like Dynamic Logic." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk06LTxRzdEtAldgZXAhbrmXUE3B5Mio2nkztyVMv92flBwR4rR26QokHNQqLHzXgz9c7sx_OMpxBL2ZYk67G007G_6A3PX7OatjZuaTB7P1cHu9gTdvLubs8ENv_rXW3sSzCMTNWYflNc7N2w3uNMuvaiQ881PEEEY=> . 


It's Mobile Not Display


Kamal Kaur, VP of Mobile & Display at social ad tech company RadiumOne, says, "...not many among my professional peers (in the world of online display) have reacted to this change. The online display industry has matured and become a lot more complex than the simple days of publishers, buyers and sellers." It's time for... mobile, which appears to be a key, strategic direction for RadiumOne. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk2nhZG90I9fnBMbH8br1iC4DMGEIWnzUwFwnmgDBdUkueFFrWUGKCk0_2GK1jmYjREU7O8T0SQkmcO9w7D-H0jLqMskGSM8kRI4ow0iA-lXkqlQP_nHB0y5ku2-ldAw893KuFl8WRk4zXadSp3D3lKgiGJlq62yT9TnUSLoO_TtJoZB9FsurVvMgJOounZWmSY=> . 


Advertising Facebook


In his first post since August, Joe Mele of Razorfish is thinking about Facebook, brands and CPMs. He thinks brands need to get their Facebook act together, "Most of the time brands are doing very little to nurture real, meaningful, business changing, customer-centric conversations with their fans. And if the final calculus of what makes marketing on Facebook valuable is the number of fans you have or the cheap CPM you were able to negotiate, then I fear we have missed the point entirely." Read what is the point <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109108282259&s=8442&e=00109VrQ7ALCk3J9CSDjuz4xP1YAm0qr3BVl_9msj2G7ZWu3VGkc5mlcraOH_vNEXHWCoPEKmCfyyWamXwCE2XMwKE-hoy2jo_Gyn4v4z7EeTJI0Ya4p4YJJMb-DbLvf30C3jbx4Hpx9QscewndcWzA_OFyP8fuh9Hd> .

SOPA Wednesday


Yesterday, in an effort to stop the "Stop Online Piracy Act" (SOPA), Internet destinations and digerati made their displeasure known that the U.S. government's attempt to stop piracy was a step in the wrong direction - if not right off a cliff - as it could subject "good" sites to the vagaries of regulation. Google took action <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_aSchmFELkOSQtxZdALKcHNkBu_Zdu5v9EAfQJitc7-qrzZ_s21p02fWUiMQCYfcqH5i6CIB_Q6sq0RBt1U2daIueJI1SCqgE7SZr3JV22bTs-ft_iIrHFZ9l9agOTLj5P8hFwkwUTN3Q==>  and Wikipedia went black <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_ZD3_KQZOPQdLsOQH864AQytOVzV9OYnWQyf-JoE0WOlxFiDFb7tOCm_2U_LdS6Qd5S6fCBV0giWfhNkoje432givbCNExyQT0H_joUdk-oKSFzl4f-juuO2JMRJGF_c6FPad-b65gZIb_CY45jxUZOOJLrcgvgQtHNK_Q71lh0FLUUT97RhW6Z8ZzS_wuciK0gZAlA8ahy1YXVOA76Zuoa2uW-UclLJ8YvADQCutzHWB4fBG34PFqP>  to name a couple. Gov't reps quickly backed down <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_Y81WMfZYvXbkK9gjaOj-QrBs6Ix8uNM0B4L_EYCL8O6YAovuVLyOML628bvWTOW0dhByMTzMH2zo0j7g-z1bSsDgVz4Bbb2bpGemubvMQjj0ZqIB1xoan_7sdN0mtbfoOd5Guv_6lQ9GXhRjjfYz4t5Sw2G15qQbPyd6CDj2QGlg6YXD39YTJxr3WezSg5LyUCgOgSofQgow9fWaXhuliLE3V7Tl5lK4g=>  from their pro-SOPA stance. And in The New York Times <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_Y81WMfZYvXbkK9gjaOj-QrBs6Ix8uNM0B4L_EYCL8O6YAovuVLyOML628bvWTOW0dhByMTzMH2zo0j7g-z1bSsDgVz4Bbb2bpGemubvMQjj0ZqIB1xoan_7sdN0mtbfoOd5Guv_6lQ9GXhRjjfYz4t5Sw2G15qQbPyd6CDj2QGlg6YXD39YTJxr3WezSg5LyUCgOgSofQgow9fWaXhuliLE3V7Tl5lK4g=> , a former movie industry lobbyist, John Feehery, chided the movie or "content" industry for its support of SOPA: "The problem for the content industry is they just don't know how to mobilize people. They have a small group of content makers, a few unions, whereas the Internet world, the social media world especially, has a tremendous reach. They can reach people in ways we never dreamed of before. This has been a real learning experience for the content world." 


Kenny As Yahoo!'s Chairman?


Is this what part of Scott Thompson's package was to step through the Yahoo! CEO door? With Jerry Yang already departed, All Things D's Kara Swisher reports four more Yahoo! board members may be given the heave-ho. Read about it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_YLb91yebx86Y1a-dQCgEQg0u4tqZ6MZczbWtruiQPQSCi_ls57B7EjD7kVy8t8oImX5EbN2nz8-1LaAjIrTv0eFlNwwpRIzJ7bFEu5vMBBMGNbQtiyHXHIuHsGinTdE28UO_O8SUUBuEx5wzsYJ2ZyoybCrYwd6SqGobcsQgN0zyt3ClIx9ixp_ekrMyCnDX9Jv4ireAWJVn2UcuUvcEg6> . Where's Yahoo! board member David Kenny in all this? The former Digitas chief and Akamai president would seem to be a good candidate to be advising - at the very least - on next steps for Yahoo! rather than exiting. Swisher thinks he could be the next chairman. 


Sell-Side Meet Buy-Side


Through a new agreement, tag manager BrightTag has made it just a little bit easier for Criteo and its clients to advertise to publisher audiences. From the BrightTag blog: "Through this BrightTag ONE partnership, shared BrightTag/Criteo clients can easily turn on Criteo data collection from within the BrightTag user interface, replacing the need to go through extensive hard-coding of individual tags." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_aDvsldmnvhXiPhH_UnPGRn5ZtQhh8JcLhbhheZLB_uefkArgKFPpHfc6OP1pDwIs-zlYAm7nu_jc8Qk-K8pSjwD-xZlMp6952hnKMz4tjwOd3ertkVw_LqeMm_8uNYQQDrqp_j79jmRv0ls15Jvx3inh8VAXrFgBRQlJEaQ_M5-w==>  Instant retargeting reach gives publishers presumably higher CPMs driven by brands' desire to reach in-market consumers via a retargeter like Criteo. 


How Are The Ad Exchanges Evolving?


Boston's North Bridge Venture Partners wants a piece of NYC's tech world - and ad exchange tech participants, too. Discussing her fund's focus, North Bridge's Dayna Grayson says, "Certainly ad tech would fall in that category. I think the industry is now ready for real automation around ad technology-both social and mobile. We're still in 1999 in mobile vs. what it's going to become. It will be used for everything. Then the question is, how are the ad exchanges today going to evolve?" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_ZAiXbDckBEyKpHMrAYwE4saIHBqOcLU6Ylizxy_J-Gq-qkhbFM_w5rHJckcvA7ent5zKMQZV7-vHP597YOSGfa9EnHZGsLJoQGWGnqVHNjzpsk9dGTcPi7SoyG6oOZKQOE9wcV020YJFjCvSGwTFV9a942LzCgzAr-HzjokXIeIqg6xF2aL0slPDWE4VwKdgRj751ykLaDb3TSur9r-HzFBaCX9v7LBMY=>  


Looking Back At Spend Forecasts


Digiday's Jack Marshall looks at the divide between what's predicted and what actually occurs when it comes to ad spending forecasts by analysts. Marshall asks if the predictions really matter and quotes Jumptap CMO Paran Johar who says, "This is what we look to analysts for - 'what's the future?' They can also help shape trends with their predictions. But you're right in that the actual 'doing' is what matters most." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_YCH0Mad0eHFMG4dMLoJFUw7TB3y_3mt_DtOnR4Adx7wjTZuUXfPu7is3gEs5obM1lErNMTJMRiMlId0AgS98w6D_sy_tSV-yRoMxBLcdLPObQh3mG5zh9fgJ-9lT9bHhOzv-U0snt0874aZoXEu0R-ZV17wxhZB0s=> . 


Video Rankings


comScore publicly released its December 2011 rankings for U.S. video ad networks - now designated as the "Ad Videos Only" list. Of note is BrightRoll's bigger reach compared to others on the partially pay-for-play list. Also, Videology (formerly TidalTV) is now part of the top 10, too, along with newcomers Auditude and Undertone. See December <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_bk09qvR08Ll7_JRfSYyOL7SaPGmaKDHnJuYrI63uWuoiVt0DnPag_KQ6DcvNJwW3qmerTv0XwxwRHwuOUm35FEn1iDX6niFLtNPP4ErgoCISFlgznKIbghwTSTk0K-TLHALfK4lXbmhlqvDo4rs-WBwUY-2od16xF4bInTqbzK-EBXW-eWTfmwVb6MnceHAXVBXNeY7Cwq1aCdC9PFvMbi_EbKlVzQHk_IOiR3AzO5wA==> . And, compare to November. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_aoWypPmzetmrDz5wi_kkBhns2d7LLmn9pEehbt0MrmLSL3bCOk6PnRDihF9MrYmnmkMk5ItbsE0F1ePJEtjktIAQ8ipY6tjyb1ayPr_wNCIOJIj1QJFdL0sdB7V_SnZ62hbQHKUzx9OP1WMlX0wtRTPd0YkuGqUsMmcQ-e-Rp1Mq7wbKM5zr_De23df6QqWXuqNtHJWBJvVVozetNdVtkkS8Pra7gZ0rgNZrnGt9t9TwRR7q3DhSp5>  


From Cookies To Gems


Adweek's Ki Mae Heussner hightlights a new company called Personal turning a consumer's data into a consumer's currency - of a sort. She writes, "Personal, using category-specific data 'gems,' can store information, from insurance policy numbers to favorite recipes to pet-sitting directions. Other 'gems' could store electronics purchases or websites a person has visited. For now, people can use the site as a quick reference or to share 'gems' with others. It's also intended to aid in the filling out of forms." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109101482829&s=8442&e=001bKlVo-VTH_ZAKfJi-wCdYp_hrSPCLAF-oMSQsx0MRBBORe8ktiMEYQkvfbELcstgSv9JiXJtunsds1gF6O9NgSuIBVrUpb3aq2BbzXthnzxzdmgzbvEqcNFuNVoBIBsqXz7rQcK_a0gvH8HsB_7sjjqAp2-dLp5HveqrQhsBiGdKK6-bDK14Yx9lHaZdfoWR> .

Yang Out


All Things D's Peter Kafka notes the official announcement on the departure of Jerry Yang from his Yahoo! board seat and, presumably, the strategic control he had of the company - though he remains a holder of a significant amount of Yahoo!'s publicly-traded shares. Yang said in the release, "As I leave the company I co-founded nearly 17 years ago, I am enthusiastic about the appointment of Scott Thompson as Chief Executive Officer and his ability, along with the entire Yahoo! leadership team, to guide Yahoo!..." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xBE94mIToYUgWijIXAnvLI84cfsI4_cYoOw6ypSGwM3I3nvSn-6ii_CxDRuqWX7V8UM3n3NFLFd5j_HE3Nvw4STrMg5AIevnvAPoNy4S92Pb47bc6DscdUTDk_rDX7WASpGD1C_8tOUIqLnXfeADUs8>  Will Yahoo! board chair Roy Bostock be next? 


The Data Of Agency HR


Former Aol-owned Pictela's marketing guru, Matt Straz, has taken the wraps off of his latest venture, Namely, and writes on the new company blog that Namely "is developing talent management software for the advertising industry," particularly agencies. The agency HR group is challenged with hiring in a rapidly innovating environment which is simultaneously buffeted by fleeting client relationships, the generous compensation structures of the startup and client-side worlds and a sideways global economy. Straz sees the effective management of people as just the first step as he posits later in his blog announcement, "The systems that we use today to manage media buying may eventually become linked to the systems that we use to manage our people." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xD2UK3sEk5a992MlTcZjzARYgXorvA-U5RHxpwEpOT5LIzHCMYqJnyByXTPLttbWcoq6PbfnnI_zKbMijNn9CqH8zF7QvUXsyP6_ICdk6c4YWoMIQ0KtROZ33JL51MxJV3aO1pZwtFeQn6MtnyGCfOY>  MediaPost's Joe Mandese notes the investor group is a who's who of media tech including Medialink's Wenda Harris Millard and Michael Kassan, Simulmedia's Dave Morgan, Buddy Media's Mike Lazerow, Admeld's Michael Barrett, former Aegis North America chief Sarah Fay and more. Read more on MediaPost <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xC-eFUHpKlhBeexQJkGC4m27Q5i6xEeke2-BDbFkRbnrGx4Yo7RJqNrQZYXxG7nWaS0yRbo-_05BrCBqkij_-a0AohuJhAp5t96FLYItwEePPvD0ZFn2cUVtJJ9fXMk0Exkjyc_MKfht-K_1ZQIRQlIZjYzzPIrzPd0jRA8RF8tdH_H_912unCBuYkgKuc0Pp6GjIfFS9IIfRL1rUrtg1fsdX1_V6CB62c=> . Namely could end up being an interesting fit with MediaOcean plans to offer plug and play capabilities for agency back office data streams and Namely's focus on unlocking the agency HR algo, if you will. Bill Wise (LinkedIn) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xCjN18Lpck0rkDLWpxuHcDhR_cfsoA2fyxZBbgzZI_SWzgaM5crVrb-bHaM2iDHFT9ivr7TrWlYbqAlAKSfyTOapj4nLnBabDhUSKHLl7F0pEvMYWxNH3Xg>  meet Matt Straz (LinkedIn) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xBO1TY64fsLfQ4W_L_vaK838ltOdJvsExnqh4i9tntsFoU48DOxphNp9cmX0LaKqcNCfL9b6uVfNw4SDr1M87VvdPAp3x83BDAPx0mv-_SHpqleLK-DrJBonUyzCI1uA1U=> . Matt Straz meet Bill Wise. And, see Namely.com <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xA-_Bj-pw_jvNvTEVrCPBpdAfsezs7-NyuXTmLQi0aMp9KHcPxdl9gP8qwzbeqs4IhX9KJon2xamWkX8o-WMmioab-vnmJRix0=> . 


Chief Optimization Officer


A flurry of C-level hirings continues in the ad ecosystem as attribution analytics company Convertro announced the appointment of Armen Avedissian as Chief Operating Officer. According to the release, Avedissian was CRO of MyLife which leveraged his media mix planning and optimization skills. CEO Jeff Zwelling said that the hiring also signals an expansion into providing attribution channels into the offline world of TV and Radio. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xBbe6YooTTqgUqvktUtKBVlzKhgNQGNjCFZ2bKwH6r9hHOFyzPwF_ddlusKsUTORl-FH9u6izYBjQ8b6CxpJxFTNrwESTkdnoNEs2l7kWHszYgTMEhQhxcSra2k9ATuyVZx5THZwHNycJiW1Or2IBnn> . 


Engaging Gains Brands


Young-Bean Song, who help drive early innovation around attribution in digital ads while he was with Atlas (eventually bought by Microsoft), takes a turn at Digiday's microphone and writes about his new company, AnalyticsDNA, and its efforts to unlock how engagement works using Solve Media CAPTCHA tech. Song summarizes, "For us to excite and surprise brand marketers, our bar needs to be double-digit gains and outliers that show the Web is as good at branding as it is at selling." Read about his findings. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xDeu3G9uFv-o1fFX7cdyaaJR3qbtpr9I9T-tJbu0y7PzqBWkSxshLgyGUB_IZsVyPgj-5M5uZsV3_XfYPBpNA6_GZUNLkocz7vZ5ebopspC5R2QQnWL6_D-Y0RwfxkPYXSM0IwLspLlljrXN0ir1uFmVKUp4lH9o_sh0vtsnIInMzLPsCZ6qo11>  


Google To Report


Google is to report Q4 2011 earnings this Thursday after the markets close. Webcast happens here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xCMmPzbIrDiXQYvnQE-Zf5EJrguWON2WPawU-KyDu2IK5xNWsF3_V3O__Qlj6LaZWeXkpeRvQb0updzplTKOId3vtXZMRo76VgimJEoD3626LovAMw0ExxS8Hv7hzfnRI8=> . Citi analyst Mark Mahaney thinks that other than some foreign currency exchange challenges, "Google's Core PC Search business still has robust, sustainable growth. We believe newer growth drivers (Mobile, Display, YouTube) are all becoming more material. And we believe market concerns over Facebook, investment ramps, and the MMI deal are somewhat overstated." GOOG's a "buy," says Mahaney. 


Do You Online AE?


A new study from Borrell Associates says that if you're an online seller, you're gold!! But, you knew that. PaidContent's Laura Hazard Owen reports on the Borrell data: "The sites that do employ online-only account execs (AEs) 'outperform those without by a factor of 2.5' in terms of gross online revenue per sales rep." This comes in the face of another trend the study unearthed- that of the uber seller who increasingly sells all channels in spite of the digital-only rep performance. Spicy stuff <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xCRBjwsLeSWgezRegcf9wpk6pVoMauUmi9-SU_R8zJyRyUtwVekkXFzcqJi_sAKBzvg0wyy21HlnzAiDoRVRpDUjk8PREiqk9tgJdMylMHaVPBRUl8fM33ovbzCxJD6YCxLej4w03uczjL-ZfOThaYvTSUdJcYw48krnjhq1Os4J91zggs0O0xbHg7FunZJPOwYrHzg_XiXS6alJ6oZU_UXQuV77nACHgQ=> . 


Publisher Audience Buyers


As web publishers consider marketing budget to build their paid subscriber list, Matt Shanahan returns to Scout Analytics' company blog and deciphers some data and suggests a best practice or two relevant to the audience buying crowd. He writes, "By focusing on the group with the highest engagement, a sales force can target their efforts to help fence-sitting fans build justification, differentiation, and ROI to go from trial to subscriber. Behavioral data reveals why conversion rates are typically low but also why conversion rates can be doubled." Read the deets. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1109095731011&s=8442&e=001SD40OeMW5xArpkxoqSgfBg-gRd_UdBfbb6sAQUXweQCTwhogMNZkeLNykGrEC-o8avyMURbAjaEtOl63uefxPMCbNV23wrnL5oID6wLUg-5EahI_JcgaXYLVudEJwaV2QOemZ2Ln3d9sMrQ3Hs0O6dWVBY2aiyL7tRCL6TUCWuu4VRTCu5bARX21UwSDYsZwu9R8AGJYpsI=>
